<div id="review_2444590751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444590751" />
    <a title="Adrea Pierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24229097-adrea-pierce"><img alt="Adrea Pierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380119920p2/24229097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444590751?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adrea Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adrea Pierce" href="/user/show/24229097-adrea-pierce">Adrea Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444590751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14512590117266217781">I began reading this book for two reasons. 1.) Because it fit the requirements of a challenge I’m in. 2.) Because it was there and I had enjoyed Shanghai Girls well enough. That said, I knew that this book revolved about Pearl and Joy and I just didn’t love either of them in the first book and because of this, I wasn’t in any rush to start this one. <br/><br/>Now that I have finished it, I would give this book 10 stars if I could. <br/><br/>It starts where Shanghai Girls ends. Joy has run away to Shanghai to find h</span>
  <span id="freeText14512590117266217781" style="display:none">I began reading this book for two reasons. 1.) Because it fit the requirements of a challenge I’m in. 2.) Because it was there and I had enjoyed Shanghai Girls well enough. That said, I knew that this book revolved about Pearl and Joy and I just didn’t love either of them in the first book and because of this, I wasn’t in any rush to start this one. <br /><br />Now that I have finished it, I would give this book 10 stars if I could. <br /><br />It starts where Shanghai Girls ends. Joy has run away to Shanghai to find her birth father and Pearl, the mother who has raised Joy from birth follows her, knowing what Joy doesn’t...that they are embarking on an extremely dangerous journey. Joy is young and naive and Pearl is not. But the fierce love of a mother for her daughter has her following Joy despite the danger. The entire book centres around the Great Leap Forward and resulting famine in China’s history. <br /><br />This book was the most suspenseful book I’ve ever read, despite not being a suspense novel at all. From start to finish, my heart was in my throat. <br /><br />Lisa See was masterful in writing these two women. I went in to the book with lukewarm feelings towards them but I came to love them very quickly. See made these women come to life and feel like my own family. I truly cared what happened to them and more times than I can count, I found myself crying over their experiences. <br /><br />I do not want to give any spoilers, but I will say this. Be warned. This book takes place is an absolutely horrific period of China’s history. It is both beautifully written and incredibly hard to read. It is not for the weak of heart. This book will haunt me for years to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14512590117266217781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_173744262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173744262" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/291863-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357103776p2/291863.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173744262?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/291863-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780679604891" href="/book/show/10577332-dreams-of-joy">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173744262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10997231603586555403">Dreams of Joy (Copied from my blog A Satisfying Affair)(Note: This review contains spoilers for Shanghai Girls by Lisa See. It would be difficult to avoid Shanghai Girls spoilers here, as Dreams of Joy is a sequel to that book, but I promise Dreams of Joy will not be spoiled here.)<br/> <br/>I have been a fan of Lisa See ever since I first read Snow Flower and the Secret Fan four years ago. I’ve found all of the books by her that I’ve read well-written and engaging, and every time I read something new fro</span>
  <span id="freeText10997231603586555403" style="display:none">Dreams of Joy (Copied from my blog A Satisfying Affair)(Note: This review contains spoilers for Shanghai Girls by Lisa See. It would be difficult to avoid Shanghai Girls spoilers here, as Dreams of Joy is a sequel to that book, but I promise Dreams of Joy will not be spoiled here.)<br /> <br />I have been a fan of Lisa See ever since I first read Snow Flower and the Secret Fan four years ago. I’ve found all of the books by her that I’ve read well-written and engaging, and every time I read something new from Lisa See I find myself raving to my friends- whose eyes quickly glaze over when they realize I’m not going to run out of air anytime soon. I was particularly excited to read Dreams of Joy, as it’s the sequel to Shanghai Girls and I’ve been at the edge of my seat since I finished that book in 2009. I had high expectations, and Dreams of Joy did not disappoint.<br /> <br />This book starts where Shanghai Girls left off. It’s 1957, and 19 year old Joy is reeling from her father’s suicide, which she blames herself for, and has just discovered that the woman she thought was her mother- Pearl- is actually her aunt, and the woman she thought was her aunt-May- is actually her birth mother. The man she called her father was not related to her by blood. Her biological father is living in communist China, and has no idea Joy even exists. Angry at her mother and aunt for lying to her, and -thinking she is responsible for the suicide of the man who raised her- angry at herself, she runs away to the People’s Republic of China to meet her biological father shortly before the start of “The Great Leap Forward”.<br /> <br />Like a lot of See’s books that I’ve read, Dreams of Joy was difficult to get into at first. I had a hard time relating to Joy at the beginning, and found myself thinking of her as an idiot for the first few chapters, and then beginning to worry about her for the next few chapters, and finally cheering her on for the last half of the book. There were times when I wanted to scream, “What are you thinking!?” for every terrible decision I saw her make. There were times when I wanted to crawl into the story, smack her across the face, then give her a big hug and a piece of bread. Meanwhile, Pearl’s actions to protect and save her daughter- and yes, while Pearl did not give birth to Joy the story makes it clear that Joy is still her daughter- are heroic, and there is a time toward the end where “the Dragon” rises to protect her family that is both heart-stopping in its intensity and beautiful in its emotion. For this reason, it is almost impossible to put this book down for the last few chapters. Though my stomach was grumbling at me and there were chores to be done, the story’s urgency leaked into the real world, and it seemed more important to know how it ended.<br /> <br />Dreams of Joy was much more intense than Shanghai Girls. The dangers inherent in the story are much more present throughout, and there is much more at stake. While Shanghai Girls was focused on carefully crafting the characters emotions and relationships, Dreams of Joy focuses more on the outer political and social sphere, and its effect on the characters, while still maintaining the heart and soul of the first book. I found Dreams of Joy to be an incredible and exciting conclusion to Shanghai Girls, and I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10997231603586555403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162226893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162226893" />
    <a title="Eileen Souza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2179211-eileen-souza"><img alt="Eileen Souza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264700002p2/2179211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162226893?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eileen Souza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eileen Souza" href="/user/show/2179211-eileen-souza">Eileen Souza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2179211-eileen-souza?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2179211-eileen-souza?shelf=asia">asia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2179211-eileen-souza?shelf=china">china</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2179211-eileen-souza?shelf=communism">communism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162226893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer662326852950712428">Finally - a proper ending to a story that started several years ago with Shanghai Girls. I have read them back to back, and I believe they must be read that way. They are two pieces of one book, not two separate novels.<br/><br/>Dreams of Joy does stand on it's own two feet - there are no extended "memory sequences" (thank god), and the story is entirely new - though still tinged with the deep feelings of the first novel. In this story we follow Joy and Pearl to China and the separate journeys that they e</span>
  <span id="freeText662326852950712428" style="display:none">Finally - a proper ending to a story that started several years ago with Shanghai Girls. I have read them back to back, and I believe they must be read that way. They are two pieces of one book, not two separate novels.<br /><br />Dreams of Joy does stand on it's own two feet - there are no extended "memory sequences" (thank god), and the story is entirely new - though still tinged with the deep feelings of the first novel. In this story we follow Joy and Pearl to China and the separate journeys that they experience there. We meet several characters from the first novel as they are 20 years later. Through Joy's eyes, we see the Great Leap Forward from the perspective of the communes, and the details and consequences of that particular campaign. Having read several fictional and biographical stories around this time in China's history, I will say that this was possibly the most graphic, and emotionally harrowing - similar to the foot binding scenes from Snow Flower, which were also the most vivid of all similar stories I have read.<br /><br />I think this is an important novel in that the characters were not above falling into the political climate, actively participating in struggle sessions, and basically acting like the sheep that follow the rest of the herd, even when it leads to complete destruction.<br /><br />I'm grateful that the ending wrapped up all of the stories from both novels in a satisfying coda.</span>
  <a data-text-id="662326852950712428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j237lpu7Ge64w63qp+z4Iq1yQavAbK+S8cbHxrejaI8ZAirEO8mz1HTguBClkIdnlJSjWJi954eyvPn/wSS5kA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HEmcMDIfp79vrNtCM4I9EFarqYbLwxT+dl60e24csu+KJk1ikm0NhaOPzrgx/kJVb01LdZMSXOs1JIpCGJtj8A==')})
  }

Willow is the only child of a destitute family, Pearl the headstrong daughter of zealous Christian missionaries. She will ultimately become the internationally renowned author Pearl S. Buck, but for now she is just a girl embarrassed by her blonde hair and enchanted by her new Chinese friend. The two embark on a friendship that will sustain both of them through one of the most tumultuous periods in Chinese history. \n\nMoving out into the world together, the two enter the intellectual fray of the times, share love interests and survive early marriages gone bad. Their shared upbringing inspires Pearl\'s novels, which celebrate the life of the Chinese peasant and will eventually earn her both a Pulitzer and a Nobel Prize. But when a civil war erupts between the Nationalists and Communists, Pearl is forced to flee the country just ahead of angry mobs. Willow, despite close ties to Mao’s inner circle, is punished for loyalty to her \'cultural imperialist\' friend. And yet, through love and loss, heartbreak and joy, exile and imprisonment, the two women remain intimately entwined. \n\nIn this ambitious new novel, Anchee Min brings to life a courageous and passionate woman who is now hailed in China as a modern heroine. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11792498996932516352">Lisa See is a Chinese-American author. Her books include <i>Snow Flower and the Secret Fan</i> (2005), <i>Dragon Bones</i>, and <i>On Gold Mountain</i>. She was named the 2001 National Woman of the Year, by the Organization of Chinese American Women. She lives in Los Angeles.<br/><br/></span>

Though both sisters wave off authority and tradition, they couldn’t be more different: Pearl is a Dragon sign, strong and stubborn, while May is a true Sheep, adorable and placid. Both are beautiful, modern, and carefree . . . until the day their father tells them that he has gambled away their wealth and that in order to repay his debts he must sell the girls as wives to suitors who have traveled from California to find Chinese brides. \n\nAs Japanese bombs fall on their beloved city, Pearl and May set out on the journey of a lifetime, one that will take them through the Chinese countryside, in and out of the clutch of brutal soldiers, and across the Pacific to the shores of America.     w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
